edX Support

For questions on course lectures, homework, tools, or materials for this course, post in the course discussion forum.

Have general questions about edX? You can find lots of helpful information in the edX FAQ.

Have a question about something specific? You can contact the edX general support team directly:



Please note: The edX support team is English speaking. While we will do our best to address your inquiry in any language, our responses will be in English.

Describe what you were doing when you encountered the issue. Include any details that will help us to troubleshoot, including error messages that you saw.

Thank You!

Thank you for your inquiry or feedback. We typically respond to a request within one business day, Monday to Friday. In the meantime, please review our detailed FAQs where most questions have already been answered.

Course Week 2: Simple Programs Problem Set 2 Introduction
<div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-vertical" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="VerticalStudentView" data-course-id="course-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017" data-request-token="7173d09d63de11e7b0fa065085eb7ade" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@vertical+block@091c114ae1b944aa81dd73b9199845cc" data-block-type="vertical"> <h2 class="hd hd-2 unit-title">Introduction</h2> <div class="bookmark-button-wrapper"> <button class="btn btn-link bookmark-button " aria-pressed="false" data-bookmark-id="infra1515,block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@vertical+block@091c114ae1b944aa81dd73b9199845cc" data-bookmarks-api-url="/api/bookmarks/v1/bookmarks/"> <span class="bookmark-text">Bookmark this page</span> </button> </div> <div class="vert-mod"> <div class="vert vert-0" data-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@html+block@c99e81ffff4546e28fecab0a0c381abd"> <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-html xmodule_display xmodule_HtmlModule" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="XBlockToXModuleShim" data-block-type="html" data-request-token="7173d09d63de11e7b0fa065085eb7ade" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@html+block@c99e81ffff4546e28fecab0a0c381abd" data-type="HTMLModule" data-course-id="course-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017"> <script type="json/xblock-args" class="xblock-json-init-args"> {"xmodule-type": "HTMLModule"} </script> <div id="edx-notes-wrapper-142527187067093402396712851597325730978" class="edx-notes-wrapper"> <div class="edx-notes-wrapper-content"><p>Each month, a credit card statement will come with the option for you to pay a minimum amount of your charge, usually 2% of the balance due. However, the credit card company earns money by charging interest on the balance that you don't pay. So even if you pay credit card payments on time, interest is still accruing on the outstanding balance.</p> <p>Say you've made a $5,000 purchase on a credit card with an 18% annual interest rate and a 2% minimum monthly payment rate. If you only pay the minimum monthly amount for a year, how much is the remaining balance?</p> <p>You can think about this in the following way.</p> <p>At the beginning of month 0 (when the credit card statement arrives), assume you owe an amount we will call [mathjaxinline]b_0[/mathjaxinline] (<i>b</i> for <i>balance</i>; subscript <i>0</i> to indicate this is the balance at month 0).</p> <p>Any payment you make during that month is deducted from the balance. Let's call the payment you make in month 0, [mathjaxinline]p_0[/mathjaxinline]. Thus, your <b>unpaid balance</b> for month 0, [mathjaxinline]ub_0[/mathjaxinline], is equal to [mathjaxinline]b_0 - p_0[/mathjaxinline].</p> <center>[mathjax]ub_0 = b_0 - p_0[/mathjax]</center> <p></p> <p>At the beginning of month 1, the credit card company will charge you interest on your unpaid balance. So if your annual interest rate is [mathjaxinline]r[/mathjaxinline], then at the beginning of month 1, your new balance is your previous unpaid balance [mathjaxinline]ub_0[/mathjaxinline], <b>plus</b> the interest on this unpaid balance for the month. In algebra, this new balance would be</p> <center>[mathjax]b_1 = ub_0 + \frac{r}{12.0}\cdot ub_0[/mathjax]</center> <p></p> <p>In month 1, we will make another payment, [mathjaxinline]p_1[/mathjaxinline]. That payment has to cover some of the interest costs, so it does not completely go towards paying off the original charge. The balance at the beginning of month 2, [mathjaxinline]b_2[/mathjaxinline], can be calculated by first calculating the unpaid balance after paying [mathjaxinline]p_1[/mathjaxinline], then by adding the interest accrued:</p> <center>[mathjax]ub_1 = b_1 - p_1[/mathjax]</center><center>[mathjax]b_2 = ub_1 + \frac{r}{12.0} \cdot ub_1[/mathjax]</center> <p></p> <p>If you choose just to pay off the minimum monthly payment each month, you will see that the compound interest will dramatically reduce your ability to lower your debt.</p> <p>Let's look at an example. If you've got a $5,000 balance on a credit card with 18% annual interest rate, and the minimum monthly payment is 2% of the current balance, we would have the following repayment schedule if you only pay the minimum payment each month:</p> <style type="text/css"><!-- table.gridtable { font-family: verdana,arial,sans-serif; font-size:11px; color:#333333; border-width: 1px; border-color: #666666; border-collapse: collapse; } table.gridtable th { border-width: 1px; padding: 8px; border-style: solid; border-color: #666666; background-color: #dedede; } table.gridtable td { border-width: 1px; padding: 8px; border-style: solid; border-color: #666666; background-color: #ffffff; } --></style> <table class="gridtable"> <tbody> <tr><th>Month</th><th>Balance</th><th>Minimum Payment</th><th>Unpaid Balance</th><th>Interest</th></tr> <tr> <td>0</td> <td>5000.00</td> <td>100 (= 5000 * 0.02)</td> <td>4900 (= 5000 - 100)</td> <td>73.50 (= 0.18/12.0 * 4900)</td> </tr> <tr> <td>1</td> <td>4973.50 (= 4900 + 73.50)</td> <td>99.47 (= 4973.50 * 0.02)</td> <td>4874.03 (= 4973.50 - 99.47)</td> <td>73.11 (= 0.18/12.0 * 4874.03)</td> </tr> <tr> <td>2</td> <td>4947.14 (= 4874.03 + 73.11)</td> <td>98.94 (= 4947.14 * 0.02)</td> <td>4848.20 (= 4947.14 - 98.94)</td> <td>72.72 (= 0.18/12.0 * 4848.20)</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <p></p> <p>You can see that a lot of your payment is going to cover interest, and if you work this through month 12, you will see that after a year, you will have paid $1165.63 and yet you will still owe $4691.11 on what was originally a $5000.00 debt. Pretty depressing!</p> <p></p></div> </div> <script type="text/javascript"> (function (require) { on the credit card&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;annualInterestRate&lt;/code&gt; - annual interest rate as a decimal&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;monthlyPaymentRate&lt;/code&gt; - minimum monthly payment rate as a decimal&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&lt;p&gt;For each month, calculate statements on the monthly payment and remaining balance. At the end of 12 months, print out the remaining balance. Be sure to print out no more than two decimal digits of accuracy - so print &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;Remaining balance: 813.41&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;instead of &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;Remaining balance: 813.4141998135 &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;So your program only prints out one thing: the remaining balance at the end of the year in the format:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;Remaining balance: 4784.0&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A summary of the required math is found below:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Monthly interest rate&lt;/strong&gt;= (Annual interest rate) / 12.0&lt;br/&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Minimum monthly payment&lt;/strong&gt; = (Minimum monthly payment rate) x (Previous balance)&lt;br/&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Monthly unpaid balance&lt;/strong&gt; = (Previous balance) - (Minimum monthly payment)&lt;br/&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Updated balance each month&lt;/strong&gt; = (Monthly unpaid balance) + (Monthly interest rate x Monthly unpaid balance) &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;We provide sample test cases below.&lt;/b&gt; We suggest you develop your code on your own machine, and make sure your code passes the sample test cases, before you paste it into the box below. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;section class=&#34;hints&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;Test Cases to Test Your Code With. Be sure to test these on your own machine - and that you get the same output! - before running your code on this webpage!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht3&#34;&gt;Click to See Problem 1 Test Cases &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht3&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note:&lt;/b&gt; Depending on where you round in this problem, your answers may be off by a few cents in either direction. Do not worry if your solution is within +/- 0.05 of the correct answer. Be sure to test these on your own machine - and that you get the same output! - before running your code on this webpage!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Test Cases:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;pre&gt; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;div id=&#34;textbox_3fa3a5ef36804834aec7adfc616d66bf_2_1&#34; class=&#34;capa_inputtype textbox cminput&#34;&gt;&lt;label class=&#34;sr problem-group-label&#34; for=&#34;cm-textarea-3fa3a5ef36804834aec7adfc616d66bf_2_1&#34;&gt;Code Editor&lt;/label&gt;&lt;textarea rows=&#34;30&#34; cols=&#34;70&#34; name=&#34;input_3fa3a5ef36804834aec7adfc616d66bf_2_1&#34; aria-label=&#34;python editor&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;answer_3fa3a5ef36804834aec7adfc616d66bf_2_1&#34; id=&#34;input_3fa3a5ef36804834aec7adfc616d66bf_2_1&#34; tabindex=&#34;0&#34; data-mode=&#34;python&#34; data-tabsize=&#34;4&#34; data-linenums=&#34;true&#34;&gt;minMonthPay = balance * monthlyPaymentRate balance -= minMonthPay # print(&#39;minMonthPay - start&#39;, minMonthPay) # print(&#39;Balance - start&#39;, balance) for i in range(12): # print(&#39;Balance top of loop&#39;, balance) balance = balance + annualInterestRate/12.0 * balance # print(&#39;Balance after adding interest&#39;, balance) minMonthPay = balance * monthlyPaymentRate # print(&#39;new minMonthPay with interest&#39;, minMonthPay) # print(&#39;Remaining balance:{0:.2f}&#39;.format(balance)) if i == 11: break balance -= minMonthPay # print(&#39;end of loop&#39;, i) print(&#39;Remaining balance:{0:.2f}&#39;.format(balance))&lt;/textarea&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;cm-editor-exit-message capa-message&#34; monthlyPaymentRate = 0.04&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;dl&gt;&lt;dt&gt;Output:&lt;/dt&gt;&lt;dd class=&#34;result-actual-output&#34;&gt;&lt;pre&gt;Remaining balance:31.38 &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/dd&gt;&lt;/dl&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;result-output result-correct&#34;&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Test Case 2&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;p&gt;balance = 484; annualInterestRate = 0.2; monthlyPaymentRate = 0.04&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;dl&gt;&lt;dt&gt;Output:&lt;/dt&gt;&lt;dd class=&#34;result-actual-output&#34;&gt;&lt;pre&gt;Remaining balance:336.21 &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/dd&gt;&lt;/dl&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;result-output result-correct&#34;&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Randomized Test Case 3&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;p&gt;balance = 249; annualInterestRate = 0.22; monthlyPaymentRate = 0.06&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;dl&gt;&lt;dt&gt;Output:&lt;/dt&gt;&lt;dd class=&#34;result-actual-output&#34;&gt;&lt;pre&gt;Remaining balance:147.37 &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/dd&gt;&lt;/dl&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;result-output result-correct&#34;&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Randomized Test Case 4&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;p&gt;balance = 276; annualInterestRate = 0.12; monthlyPaymentRate = 0.05&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;dl&gt;&lt;dt&gt;Output:&lt;/dt&gt;&lt;dd class=&#34;result-actual-output&#34;&gt;&lt;pre&gt;Remaining balance:168.05 &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/dd&gt;&lt;/dl&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;section class=&#34;hints&#34;&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Hints&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;Only two decimal digits of accuracy?&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;Use the &lt;code&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;http://docs.python.org/library/functions.html#round&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34;&gt;round&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/code&gt; function at the end of your code!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht2&#34;&gt;How to think about this problem?&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht2&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;To help you get started, here is a rough outline of the stages you should probably follow in writing your code:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;For each month:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Compute the monthly payment, based on the previous month&amp;#8217;s balance.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Update the outstanding balance by removing the payment, then charging interest on the result.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Output the month, the minimum monthly payment and the remaining balance.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Keep track of the total amount of paid over all the past months so far.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Print out the result statement with the total amount paid and the remaining balance.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;Use these ideas to guide the creation of your code.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;section class=&#34;hints&#34;&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Important&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;imp1&#34;&gt;Only hit &#34;Check&#34; once per submission. You only get 30 checks per problem.&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;imp1&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;** Our automatic grader may take a few minutes to respond with feedback. If you hit &#34;Check&#34; multiple times, you will lose a check for every press of the button.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;** If you&#39;re unfamiliar with how our autograder works, first try out one of the infinite check problems in the Functions lecture sequence.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;** Please be judicious with your checks, as we are unable to give you more than 30 checks. However this should be more than sufficient: if you do your code development in your local environment, and ensure you can pass our test cases, you should not require more than a few checks once you paste your working, tested code into our code box.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;If you believe you have correct code but it is marked incorrect after clicking &#34;Check&#34;...&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;** After you submit your code, you can see every test case the graders runs on your code. They compare what your code outputs with what our answer code is supposed to output. Click the small link titled &#34;See Full Output&#34; below the Test Results header.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;&#34;Staff Debug: L397 Error&#34; means your code has an infinite loop...&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;** Clicking Check may give you the error:&lt;br/&gt; &lt;code&gt;There was a problem running your solution (Staff debug: L379).&lt;/code&gt; &lt;code&gt;We couldn&#39;t run your solution (Staff debug: L397).&lt;/code&gt;. &lt;br/&gt;This means your code is taking too long or has an infinite loop. Test your code with more unique test cases, such as very large or very small values. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;Do not define your own values&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;** For problems such as these, do not include &lt;code&gt;input&lt;/code&gt; statements or define variables we told you would be given. Our automated testing will provide values for you - so write your code in the following box assuming those variables are already defined. The code you paste into the following box &lt;b&gt;should not&lt;/b&gt; specify the values for the variables &lt;code&gt;balance&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;annualInterestRate&lt;/code&gt;, or &lt;code&gt;monthlyPaymentRate&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;action&#34;&gt; &lt;input type=&#34;hidden&#34; name=&#34;problem_id&#34; value=&#34;Problem 1 - Paying Debt off in a Year&#34; /&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;submit-attempt-container&#34;&gt; &lt;button type=&#34;button&#34; class=&#34;submit btn-brand&#34; data-submitting=&#34;Submitting&#34; data-value=&#34;Submit&#34; data-should-enable-submit-button=&#34;False&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;submission_feedback_3fa3a5ef36804834aec7adfc616d66bf&#34; disabled&gt; &lt;span class=&#34;submit-label&#34;&gt;Submit&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/button&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;submission-feedback&#34; id=&#34;submission_feedback_3fa3a5ef36804834aec7adfc616d66bf&#34;&gt; You have used 4 of 30 attempts &lt;span class=&#34;sr&#34;&gt;Some problems have options such as save, reset, hints, or show answer. data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="XBlockToXModuleShim" data-block-type="problem" data-request-token="7173d09d63de11e7b0fa065085eb7ade" data-runtime-version="1" aria-labelledby="aaabd7448b6546b28edfdee51eda8861-problem-title" data-problem-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@aaabd7448b6546b28edfdee51eda8861" data-problem-total-possible="15.0" data-attempts-used="2" data-content=" &lt;h3 class=&#34;hd hd-3 problem-header&#34; id=&#34;aaabd7448b6546b28edfdee51eda8861-problem-title&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@aaabd7448b6546b28edfdee51eda8861-problem-progress&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt; Problem 2 - Paying Debt Off in a Year &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@aaabd7448b6546b28edfdee51eda8861-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;p&gt;Now write a program that calculates the minimum &lt;b&gt;fixed&lt;/b&gt; monthly payment needed in order pay off a credit card balance within 12 months. By a fixed monthly payment, we mean a single number which does not change each month, but instead is a constant amount that will be paid each month.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In this problem, we will &lt;i&gt;not&lt;/i&gt; be dealing with a minimum monthly payment rate.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The following variables contain values as described below:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;balance&lt;/code&gt; - the outstanding balance on the credit card&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;annualInterestRate&lt;/code&gt; - annual interest rate as a decimal&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&lt;p&gt; The program should print out one line: the lowest monthly payment that will pay off all debt in under 1 year, for example: &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;Lowest Payment: 180 &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Assume that the interest is compounded monthly according to the balance at the end of the month (after the payment for that month is made). The monthly payment must be a multiple of $10 and is the same for all months. Notice that it is possible for the balance to become negative using this payment scheme, which is okay. A summary of the required math is found below:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Monthly interest rate&lt;/strong&gt; = (Annual interest rate) / 12.0&lt;br/&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Monthly unpaid balance&lt;/strong&gt; = (Previous balance) - (Minimum fixed monthly payment)&lt;br/&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Updated balance each month&lt;/strong&gt; = (Monthly unpaid balance) + (Monthly interest rate x Monthly unpaid balance) &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;section class=&#34;hints&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Test Cases to Test Your Code With.&lt;/b&gt; Be sure to test these on your own machine - and that you get the same output! - before running your code on this webpage!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht3&#34;&gt;Click to See Problem 2 Test Cases &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht3&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;Be sure to test these on your own machine - and that you get the same output! - before running your code on this webpage!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Test Cases:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;code&gt; Test Case 1: balance = 3329 annualInterestRate = 0.2 Result Your Code Should Generate: ------------------- Lowest Payment: 310 &lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;code&gt; Test Case 2: balance = 4773 annualInterestRate = 0.2 Result Your Code Should Generate: ------------------- Lowest Payment: 440 &lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;code&gt; Test Case 3: balance = 3926 annualInterestRate = 0.2 Result Your Code Should Generate: ------------------- Lowest Payment: 360 &lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;div id=&#34;textbox_aaabd7448b6546b28edfdee51eda8861_2_1&#34; class=&#34;capa_inputtype textbox cminput&#34;&gt;&lt;label class=&#34;sr problem-group-label&#34; for=&#34;cm-textarea-aaabd7448b6546b28edfdee51eda8861_2_1&#34;&gt;Code Editor&lt;/label&gt;&lt;textarea rows=&#34;30&#34; cols=&#34;70&#34; name=&#34;input_aaabd7448b6546b28edfdee51eda8861_2_1&#34; aria-label=&#34;python editor&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;answer_aaabd7448b6546b28edfdee51eda8861_2_1&#34; id=&#34;input_aaabd7448b6546b28edfdee51eda8861_2_1&#34; tabindex=&#34;0&#34; data-mode=&#34;python&#34; data-tabsize=&#34;4&#34; data-linenums=&#34;true&#34;&gt;minFixed = 0 original_balance = balance while balance &amp;gt;= 0: balance = original_balance minFixed += 10 for i in range(12): balance -= minFixed balance += balance * annualInterestRate//12 print(minFixed)&lt;/textarea&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;cm-editor-exit-message capa-message&#34; annualInterestRate = 0.18&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;dl&gt;&lt;dt&gt;Output:&lt;/dt&gt;&lt;dd class=&#34;result-actual-output&#34;&gt;&lt;pre&gt;290 &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/dd&gt;&lt;/dl&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;result-output result-correct&#34;&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Randomized Test Case 12&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;p&gt;balance = 3162; annualInterestRate = 0.04&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;dl&gt;&lt;dt&gt;Output:&lt;/dt&gt;&lt;dd class=&#34;result-actual-output&#34;&gt;&lt;pre&gt;270 &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/dd&gt;&lt;/dl&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;section class=&#34;hints&#34;&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Hints&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;Hint: How to think about this problem? &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;Start with $10 payments per month and calculate whether the balance will be paid off in a year this way (be sure to take into account the interest accrued each month). &lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;If $10 monthly payments are insufficient to pay off the debt within a year, increase the monthly payment by $10 and repeat. &lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht2&#34;&gt;Hint: A way of structuring your code&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht2&#34;&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;If you are struggling with how to structure your code, think about the following: &lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;Given an initial balance, what code would compute the balance at the end of the year?&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Now imagine that we try our initial balance with a monthly payment of $10. If there is a balance remaining at the end of the year, how could we write code that would reset the balance to the initial balance, increase the payment by $10, and try again (using the same code!) to compute the balance at the end of the year, to see if this new payment value is large enough.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht2a&#34;&gt;I&#39;m still confused!&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht2a&#34;&gt; A good way to implement this problem will be to use a loop structure. You may want to refresh your understanding of &lt;b&gt;while&lt;/b&gt; loops. Think hard about how the program will know when it has found a good minimum monthly payment value - when a good value is found, the loop can terminate. &lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt; &lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Be careful - you don&#39;t want to overwrite the original value of &lt;code&gt;balance&lt;/code&gt;. You&#39;ll need to save that value somehow for later reference!&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Reminder:&lt;/b&gt; Only hit &#34;Check&#34; once per submission. We are unable to give you more than 30 checks.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;section class=&#34;hints&#34;&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Important&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;imp1&#34;&gt;Only hit &#34;Check&#34; once per submission. You only get 30 checks per problem.&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;imp1&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;** Our automatic grader may take a few minutes to respond with feedback. If you hit &#34;Check&#34; multiple times, you will lose a check for every press of the button.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;** If you&#39;re unfamiliar with how our autograder works, first try out one of the infinite check problems in the Functions lecture sequence.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;** Please be judicious with your checks, as we are unable to give you more than 30 checks. However this should be more than sufficient: if you do your code development in your local environment, and ensure you can pass our test cases, you should not require more than a few checks once you paste your working, tested code into our code box.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;If you believe you have correct code but it is marked incorrect after clicking &#34;Check&#34;...&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;** After you submit your code, you can see every test case the graders runs on your code. <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-vertical" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="VerticalStudentView" data-course-id="course-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017" data-request-token="7173d09d63de11e7b0fa065085eb7ade" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@vertical+block@15f3736c24e043a580e146f5f39cdcb4" data-block-type="vertical"> <h2 class="hd hd-2 unit-title">Problem 3</h2> <div class="bookmark-button-wrapper"> <button class="btn btn-link bookmark-button " aria-pressed="false" data-bookmark-id="infra1515,block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@vertical+block@15f3736c24e043a580e146f5f39cdcb4" data-bookmarks-api-url="/api/bookmarks/v1/bookmarks/"> <span class="bookmark-text">Bookmark this page</span> </button> </div> <div class="vert-mod"> <div class="vert vert-0" data-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@a0b78fd689564e82b9da6a8f266fa0ef"> <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-problem xmodule_display xmodule_CapaModule" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="XBlockToXModuleShim" data-block-type="problem" data-request-token="7173d09d63de11e7b0fa065085eb7ade" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@a0b78fd689564e82b9da6a8f266fa0ef" data-type="Problem" data-course-id="course-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017"> <script type="json/xblock-args" class="xblock-json-init-args"> {"xmodule-type": "Problem"} </script> <div id="problem_a0b78fd689564e82b9da6a8f266fa0ef" class="problems-wrapper" role="group" aria-labelledby="a0b78fd689564e82b9da6a8f266fa0ef-problem-title" data-problem-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@a0b78fd689564e82b9da6a8f266fa0ef" data-url="/courses/course-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017/xblock/block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@a0b78fd689564e82b9da6a8f266fa0ef/handler/xmodule_handler" data-problem-score="20.0" data-problem-total-possible="20.0" data-attempts-used="1" data-content=" &lt;h3 class=&#34;hd hd-3 problem-header&#34; id=&#34;a0b78fd689564e82b9da6a8f266fa0ef-problem-title&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@a0b78fd689564e82b9da6a8f266fa0ef-problem-progress&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt; Problem 3 - Using Bisection Search to Make the Program Faster &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@a0b78fd689564e82b9da6a8f266fa0ef-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;p&gt;You&#39;ll notice that in Problem 2, your monthly payment had to be a multiple of $10. Why did we make it that way? You can try running your code locally so that the payment can be any dollar and cent amount (in other words, the monthly payment is a multiple of $0.01). Does your code still work? It should, but you may notice that your code runs more slowly, especially in cases with very large balances and interest rates. (Note: when your code is running on our servers, there are limits on the amount of computing time each submission is allowed, so your observations from running this experiment on the grading system might be limited to an error message complaining about too much time taken.)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt; Well then, how can we calculate a more accurate fixed monthly payment than we did in Problem 2 without running into the problem of slow code? We can make this program run faster using a technique introduced in lecture - bisection search!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The following variables contain values as described below:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;balance&lt;/code&gt; - the outstanding balance on the credit card&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;annualInterestRate&lt;/code&gt; - annual interest rate as a decimal&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&lt;p&gt; To recap the problem: we are searching for the smallest monthly payment such that we can pay off the entire balance within a year. What is a reasonable &lt;b&gt;lower bound&lt;/b&gt; for this payment value? $0 is the obvious anwer, but you can do better than that. If there was no interest, the debt can be paid off by monthly payments of one-twelfth of the original balance, so we must pay at least this much every month. One-twelfth of the original balance is a good lower bound.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;What is a good &lt;b&gt;upper bound&lt;/b&gt;? Imagine that instead of paying monthly, we paid off the entire balance at the end of the year. What we ultimately pay must be greater than what we would&#39;ve paid in monthly installments, because the interest was compounded on the balance we didn&#39;t pay off each month. So a good upper bound for the monthly payment would be one-twelfth of the balance, &lt;i&gt;after&lt;/i&gt; having its interest compounded monthly for an entire year.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In short:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Monthly interest rate&lt;/strong&gt; = (Annual interest rate) / 12.0&lt;br/&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Monthly payment lower bound&lt;/strong&gt; = Balance / 12&lt;br/&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Monthly payment upper bound&lt;/strong&gt; = (Balance x (1 + Monthly interest rate)&lt;sup&gt;12&lt;/sup&gt;) / 12.0 &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Write a program that uses these bounds and bisection search (for more info check out &lt;a href=&#34;http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bisection_method&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34;&gt;the Wikipedia page on bisection search&lt;/a&gt;) to find the smallest monthly payment &lt;em&gt;to the cent&lt;/em&gt; (no more multiples of $10) such that we can pay off the debt within a year. Try it out with large inputs, and notice how fast it is (try the same large inputs in your solution to Problem 2 to compare!). Produce the same return value as you did in Problem 2.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Note that if you do not use bisection search, your code will not run - your code only has 30 seconds to run on our servers.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;section class=&#34;hints&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Test Cases to Test Your Code With.&lt;/b&gt; Be sure to test these on your own machine - and that you get the same output! - before running your code on this webpage!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht3l&#34;&gt;Click to See Problem 3 Test Cases &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht3&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note:&lt;/b&gt; The automated tests are leinient - if your answers are off by a few cents in either direction, your code is OK. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Be sure to test these on your own machine - and that you get the same output! - before running your code on this webpage!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Test Cases:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;code&gt; Test Case 1: balance = 320000 annualInterestRate = 0.2 Result Your Code Should Generate: ------------------- Lowest Payment: 29157.09 &lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;code&gt; Test Case 2: balance = 999999 annualInterestRate = 0.18 Result Your Code Should Generate: ------------------- Lowest Payment: 90325.03 &lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;div id=&#34;textbox_a0b78fd689564e82b9da6a8f266fa0ef_2_1&#34; class=&#34;capa_inputtype textbox cminput&#34;&gt;&lt;label class=&#34;sr problem-group-label&#34; for=&#34;cm-textarea-a0b78fd689564e82b9da6a8f266fa0ef_2_1&#34;&gt;Code Editor&lt;/label&gt;&lt;textarea rows=&#34;30&#34; cols=&#34;70&#34; name=&#34;input_a0b78fd689564e82b9da6a8f266fa0ef_2_1&#34; aria-label=&#34;python editor&#34; "course\u002Dv1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017"; function DiscussionInlineBlock(runtime, element) { 'use strict'; var el = $(element).find('.discussion-module'); new DiscussionInlineView({ el: el, readOnly: Introduction

Each month, a credit card statement will come with the option for you to pay a minimum amount of your charge, usually 2% of the balance due. However, the credit card company earns money by charging interest on the balance that you don't pay. So even if you pay credit card payments on time, interest is still accruing on the outstanding balance.

Say you've made a $5,000 purchase on a credit card with an 18% annual interest rate and a 2% minimum monthly payment rate. If you only pay the minimum monthly amount for a year, how much is the remaining balance?

You can think about this in the following way.

At the beginning of month 0 (when the credit card statement arrives), assume you owe an amount we will call b0 (b for balance; subscript 0 to indicate this is the balance at month 0).

Any payment you make during that month is deducted from the balance. Let's call the payment you make in month 0, p0. Thus, your unpaid balance for month 0, ub0, is equal to b0p0.

ub0=b0p0

At the beginning of month 1, the credit card company will charge you interest on your unpaid balance. So if your annual interest rate is r, then at the beginning of month 1, your new balance is your previous unpaid balance ub0, plus the interest on this unpaid balance for the month. In algebra, this new balance would be

b1=ub0+r12.0ub0

In month 1, we will make another payment, p1. That payment has to cover some of the interest costs, so it does not completely go towards paying off the original charge. The balance at the beginning of month 2, b2, can be calculated by first calculating the unpaid balance after paying p1, then by adding the interest accrued:

ub1=b1p1
b2=ub1+r12.0ub1

If you choose just to pay off the minimum monthly payment each month, you will see that the compound interest will dramatically reduce your ability to lower your debt.

Let's look at an example. If you've got a $5,000 balance on a credit card with 18% annual interest rate, and the minimum monthly payment is 2% of the current balance, we would have the following repayment schedule if you only pay the minimum payment each month:

MonthBalanceMinimum PaymentUnpaid BalanceInterest
0 5000.00 100 (= 5000 * 0.02) 4900 (= 5000 - 100) 73.50 (= 0.18/12.0 * 4900)
1 4973.50 (= 4900 + 73.50) 99.47 (= 4973.50 * 0.02) 4874.03 (= 4973.50 - 99.47) 73.11 (= 0.18/12.0 * 4874.03)
2 4947.14 (= 4874.03 + 73.11) 98.94 (= 4947.14 * 0.02) 4848.20 (= 4947.14 - 98.94) 72.72 (= 0.18/12.0 * 4848.20)

You can see that a lot of your payment is going to cover interest, and if you work this through month 12, you will see that after a year, you will have paid $1165.63 and yet you will still owe $4691.11 on what was originally a $5000.00 debt. Pretty depressing!
